The problem occurs during autofs unmount of a child mount. Let me re-read the bug report symptoms and look at the nfs3_rpc_wrapper code more carefully.\n\nActually, looking at the nfs3_rpc_wrapper code again, I think I understand the real bug now!\n\n```c\nstatic int\nnfs3_rpc_wrapper(struct rpc_clnt *clnt, struct rpc_message *msg, int flags)\n{\n    int res;\n    do {\n        res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n        if (res != -EJUKEBOX)\n            break;\n        freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n        res = -ERESTARTSYS;\n    } while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\n    return res;\n}\n```\n\nThe bug is on line 39! After sleeping, the code unconditionally sets `res = -ERESTARTSYS`. This is WRONG because:\n\n1. If the sleep completes normally (without signal), fatal_signal_pending() returns false\n2. The while loop condition `!fatal_signal_pending(current)` evaluates to TRUE\n3. We loop back and call rpc_call_sync again\n4. res gets overwritten by the new RPC result\n5. We check if it's JUKEBOX again\n\nBut the issue is: what if between the sleep waking up and checking fatal_signal_pending, the process gets a signal? Or more importantly, what if freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe() returns because of being killed, not because of timeout?\n\nActually, I think the real issue is simpler. Let me look at what `freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe` does and when it returns with an error.Actually, looking more carefully, I think the REAL bug is this:When the while condition `!fatal_signal_pending(current)` is false (meaning a fatal signal IS pending), we exit the loop and return `res`, which was set to `-ERESTARTSYS`.\n\n\nThe problem is that we're setting `res = -ERESTARTSYS` unconditionally after every sleep, regardless of whether a signal actually occurred. So when the first RPC call returns -EJUKEBOX, we sleep, then always assign -ERESTARTSYS to res. If no signal is pending, the loop continues and res gets overwritten by the next rpc_call_sync result. But if a signal IS pending, we exit and return -ERESTARTSYS, which is the intended behavior. The real issue is that we're not checking whether the sleep itself was interrupted by a signal before unconditionally setting this error code. Looking at the NFS4 implementation might reveal how this should be handled correctly. The key difference could be in how the signal check is sequenced relative to the restart logic, or there might be a missing condition that prevents the restart in certain Now I see the difference clearly!\n\n**In nfs4proc.c (correct):**\n```c\nstatic int nfs4_delay(struct rpc_clnt *clnt, long *timeout)\n{\n    int res = 0;    might_sleep();    freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(...);\n    if (fatal_signal_pending(current))\n        res = -ERESTARTSYS;\n    return res;\n}```\nThe logic is:\n1. Initialize res to 0\n2. Sleep\n3. IF a fatal signal is pending, set res to -ERESTARTSYS\n4. Return res (either 0 if no signal, or -ERESTARTSYS if signal)\n\n**In nfs3proc.c (incorrect):**\n```c\nstatic int nfs3_rpc_wrapper(struct rpc_clnt *clnt, struct rpc_message *msg, int flags)\n{\n    int res;\n    do {\n        res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n        if (res != -EJUKEBOX)\n            break;\n        freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n        res = -ERESTARTSYS;                     // <-- ALWAYS SET\n    } while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\n    return res;\n}```\n\nThe bug is on line 39! After sleeping, the code UNCONDITIONALLY sets `res = -ERESTARTSYS` without first checking if a signal actually occurred!\n\nThis means:\n- If the sleep times out normally (no signal), res is set to -ERESTARTSYS\n- Then the loop condition `while (!fatal_signal_pending(current))` is checked\n- If no signal is pending, the loop continues back to rpc_call_sync\n- But importantly, res is already set to -ERESTARTSYSActually, wait. Let me trace through this one more time with a concrete scenario:\n\n\nWhen the sleep completes normally without any signal, res gets unconditionally set to -ERESTARTSYS. The loop then checks if a signal is pending—if none is, it loops back and rpc_call_sync overwrites res with a new result. But the problem is that res was unnecessarily set to an error code even though the sleep succeeded normally.\n\nThe real issue emerges when a fatal signal arrives after the sleep but before the fatal_signal_pending check. In that case, res would already be -ERESTARTSYS from the unconditional assignment, and the loop condition would fail, causing the function to return -ERESTARTSYS even though the sleep itself completed successfully.\n\nLooking at the loop structure more carefully: the condition `while (!fatal_signal_pending(current))` means we continue looping only if no fatal signal is pending. Once a signal arrives, we exit and return whatever's in res. The problem is that res gets set to -ERESTARTSYS before checking for signals, so if a signal happens to arrive at just the right moment, we're returning an error code that doesn't accurately reflect what actually happened during the sleep.\n\nThe NFS3 implementation differs from NFS4 in how it handles this scenario—NFS3 unconditionally assigns -ERESTARTSYS to res, whereas NFS4 takes a different
